Now I think I've found an issue. Look at line 124 in register.go:\n\n```go\nerr = params.Storage.UpsertU2FRegisterChallenge(params.StorageKey, c)\n```\n\nThis stores the registration challenge with just the `StorageKey` (which is the username). But wait, let me look at the registration storage implementation again. On line 92-93:\n\n```go\nfunc (s inMemoryRegistrationStorage) UpsertU2FRegisterChallenge(key string, c *Challenge) error {\n    return s.challenges.Set(key, c, int(inMemoryChallengeTTL.Seconds()))\n}\n```\n\nAnd looking at the `AddMFADeviceRegisterChallenge` function in grpcserver.go at line 1352-1356:\n\n```go\nchallenge, err := u2f.RegisterInit(u2f.RegisterInitParams{\n    StorageKey: user,\n    AppConfig:  *u2fConfig,\n    Storage:    u2fStorage,\n})\n```\n\nSo the registration storage key is just the username! This means if two registration challenges are initiated (e.g., user tries to register two U2F devices in a row), the second call to `UpsertU2FRegisterChallenge` will **overwrite** the first challenge!\n\nBut that's during registration, not authentication. Let me look back at the authentication side.\n\nLooking at AuthenticateInit in authenticate.go at line 140:\n\n```go\nif err = params.Storage.UpsertU2FSignChallenge(params.StorageKey, params.Dev.Id, challenge); err != nil {\n    return nil, trace.Wrap(err)\n}\n```\n\nThis takes both the `StorageKey` (username) and the `Dev.Id` (device ID), so it should be fine for authentication - it stores one challenge per device.\n\n\nNow checking where the authentication storage gets initialized in grpcserver.go at line 1283, a single `u2fStorage` instance is created and passed through to `mfaAuthChallenge`. Within that function, `AuthenticateInit` is called for each registered device, storing a separate challenge per device ID.\n\nLooking back at the test around line 181, it expects exactly one U2F challenge in the request. The test scenario has one existing device (\"u2f-dev\") and attempts to register another, so the challenge should only cover the existing device. The test name \"fail U2F auth challenge\" at line 174 confirms this is testing the failure case where an unregistered device tries to authenticate—which is the expected behavior. But there's something else to consider here.\n\nScanning through the addTests section (lines 79-308), I notice the test suite covers adding an initial TOTP device, adding a U2F device, and then several failure scenarios: attempting to add another U2F with the wrong device, attempting to add another U2F with wrong TOTP credentials, and similar failures for TOTP registration. However, there's no successful test for registering multiple U2F devices. The final expected state at line 327 shows only [\"totp-dev\", \"u2f-dev\"], suggesting the test never actually completes a second U2F registration.\n\nThis points to a potential bug: when RegisterInit is called multiple times for the same user, the challenge storage uses only the username as the key, not a per-device identifier. Looking at the RegisterInit function in register.go, each call to UpsertU2FRegisterChallenge with the same StorageKey overwrites the previous challenge. So if a user initiates registration for a second U2F device before completing the first one, the new challenge replaces the old one, making it impossible to complete the original registration.\n\nIn RegisterVerify, the code retrieves the challenge using the same key and attempts to verify the response against it. If the challenge was overwritten during a concurrent registration attempt, the verification would fail because the response won't match the current stored challenge. This suggests the storage mechanism needs to be redesigned to handle multiple concurrent registration flows per user, perhaps by including a device identifier or timestamp in the storage key.\n\nHowever, looking back at the issue description—\"during login, only one device is recognized\"—this points to a different problem. The issue occurs when users authenticate, not when they register. The authentication flow should present challenges for all registered devices, allowing users to choose which token to use. At line 876:```go\nres.Challenges = append(res.Challenges, *ch)```And then at line 877-879:```go\nif res.AuthenticateChallenge == nil {\n    res.AuthenticateChallenge = ch\n}```So if there are multiple devices, `res.Challenges` will have all of them, but `res.AuthenticateChallenge` will only have the first one!But that should be fine because the comment at line 831-833 says:```// Before 6.0 teleport would only send 1 U2F challenge. Embed the old// challenge for compatibility with older clients. All new clients should// ignore this and read Challenges instead.```So the `Challenges` slice should have all devices, and clients should use that.So if the code looks correct, maybe the bug is in a different place. The handler reads the JSON request, validates the credentials, and returns the U2F sign request to the client.\n\nThe actual signing logic happens in the `U2FSignRequest` function (lines 839-880), which iterates through all registered devices and generates a challenge for each one. However, I notice the `U2FAuthenticateChallenge` struct contains a comment indicating that before version 6.0, Teleport only sent a single challenge for backward compatibility with older clients. This historical limitation suggests there may have been an earlier implementation that restricted challenges to just one device.\n\nThe fix for this was supposed to introduce the `Challenges` field to support multiple devices, but the implementation might be incomplete. I should write a regression test to verify the behavior: create a user, register two U2F devices, request a login challenge, and confirm both devices appear in the response.
